<p><b>Madeira</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">ɪər</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>, -<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">ɛər</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i>mə-<b>DEER</b>-ə</i></small></a>, <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i>-<b>DAIR</b>-ə</i></small></a>; <small>Portuguese: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[mɐˈðejɾɐ, -ˈðɐj-]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> situated in the north <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, southwest of Portugal. Its total population was estimated in 2011 at 267,785. The capital of Madeira is <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a>, located on the main island's south coast.</p>
<p>The archipelago is just under 400 kilometres (250 mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>. Since 1976, the archipelago has been one of the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_Portugal" title="Autonomous regions of Portugal">autonomous regions of Portugal</a> (the other being the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, located to the northwest). It includes the islands of <a href="/wiki/Madeira#Madeira_Island" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Island" title="Porto Santo Island">Porto Santo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Desertas_Islands" title="Desertas Islands">Desertas</a>, administered together with the separate archipelago of the <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>. The region has political and administrative autonomy through the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Regions_of_Portugal#Constitution" title="Autonomous Regions of Portugal">Administrative Political Statue of the Autonomous Region of Madeira</a> provided for in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constitution" title="Portuguese Constitution">Portuguese Constitution</a>. The autonomous region is an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, having pronounced status as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outermost_regions_of_the_European_Union" title="Outermost regions of the European Union">outermost region</a> of the European Union, as detailed in Article 299-2 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaty of the European Union">Treaty of the European Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madeira was claimed by Portuguese sailors in the service of Prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a> in 1419 and settled after 1420. The archipelago is considered to be the first territorial discovery of the exploratory period of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1415%E2%80%931542)#Ships" title="History of Portugal (1415–1542)">Portuguese Age of Discovery</a>, which extended from 1415 to 1542.</p>
<p>Today, it is a popular year-round <a href="/wiki/Resort" title="Resort">resort</a>, being visited every year by about one million tourists,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> three times its population. The region is noted for its <a href="/wiki/Madeira_wine" title="Madeira wine">Madeira wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomy</a>, historical and cultural value, <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a>, landscapes (<a href="/wiki/Laurel_forest" title="Laurel forest">Laurel forest</a>) which are classified as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, and embroidery artisans. Its annual New Year celebrations feature the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fireworks_show" title="Fireworks show">fireworks show</a> in the world, as officially recognised by <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The main harbour in Funchal is the leading Portuguese port in cruise liner dockings,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> being an important stopover for commercial and trans-Atlantic passenger cruises between Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and North Africa. Madeira is the second richest region of Portugal by GDP per capita, only surpassed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon_Region" title="Lisbon Region">Lisbon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Madeira" title="History of Madeira">History of Madeira</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration">Exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a> in his <i><a href="/wiki/Parallel_Lives" title="Parallel Lives">Parallel Lives</a></i> (<i>Sertorius</i>, 75 AD) referring to the military commander <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Sertorius" title="Quintus Sertorius">Quintus Sertorius</a> (d. 72 BC), relates that after his return to <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>, he met sailors who spoke of idyllic Atlantic islands: "The islands are said to be two in number separated by a very narrow strait and lie 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Furlong" title="Furlong">furlongs</a> (2,011.68 km) from Africa. They are called the Isles of the Blessed...".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Archeological evidence suggests that the islands may have been visited by the Vikings sometime between 900 and 1030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legend">Legend</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Legend">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward III of England</a>, lovers <a href="/wiki/Robert_Machin" title="Robert Machin">Robert Machim</a> and Anna d'Arfet were said to flee from England to France in 1346. They were driven off their course by a violent storm and their ship went aground along the coast of an island that may have been Madeira. Later this legend was the basis of the naming of the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machico" title="Machico">Machico</a>, in memory of the young lovers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery">Discovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Discovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Knowledge of some Atlantic islands, such as Madeira, existed before their formal discovery and settlement, as the islands were shown on maps as early as 1339.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DNB_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-DNB-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Funchal_(_Portugal_)13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3828" data-file-width="5184" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Funchal_%28_Portugal_%2913.jpg/180px-Funchal_%28_Portugal_%2913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Funchal_%28_Portugal_%2913.jpg/270px-Funchal_%28_Portugal_%2913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Funchal_%28_Portugal_%2913.jpg/360px-Funchal_%28_Portugal_%2913.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Funchal_(_Portugal_)13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Gon%C3%A7alves_Zarco" title="João Gonçalves Zarco">João Gonçalves Zarco</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1418, two captains under service to Prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Gon%C3%A7alves_Zarco" title="João Gonçalves Zarco">João Gonçalves Zarco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trist%C3%A3o_Vaz_Teixeira" title="Tristão Vaz Teixeira">Tristão Vaz Teixeira</a>, were driven off course by a storm to an island which they named <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Island" title="Porto Santo Island">Porto Santo</a> (English: <i>holy harbour</i>) in gratitude for divine deliverance from a shipwreck. The following year, an organised expedition, under the captaincy of Zarco, Vaz Teixeira, and <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Perestrello" title="Bartolomeu Perestrello">Bartolomeu Perestrello</a>, traveled to the island to claim it on behalf of the Portuguese Crown. Subsequently, the new settlers observed "a heavy black cloud suspended to the southwest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Their investigation revealed it to be the larger island they called Madeira.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg/180px-S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg/270px-S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg/360px-S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A9_church_Funchal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Funchal" title="Cathedral of Funchal">Cathedral of Funchal</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Tower" title="Tower">tower</a> of 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic style</a> in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first Portuguese settlers began colonizing the islands around 1420 or 1425.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Grain production began to fall and the ensuing crisis forced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a> to order other commercial crops to be planted so that the islands could be profitable.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These specialised plants, and their associated industrial technology, created one of the major revolutions on the islands and fuelled Portuguese industry. Following the introduction of the first water-driven sugar mill on Madeira, sugar production increased to over 6,000 <i>arrobas</i> (an <i>arroba</i> was equal to 11 to 12 kilograms) by 1455,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crosby2015_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crosby2015-19">[19]</a></sup> using advisers from <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and financed by <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> capital. (Genoa acted as an integral part of the island economy until the 17th century.) The accessibility of Madeira attracted Genoese and <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flemish</a> traders, who were keen to bypass <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetian</a> monopolies.</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"By 1480 <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> had some seventy ships engaged in the Madeira sugar trade, with the refining and distribution concentrated in Antwerp. By the 1490s Madeira had overtaken <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> as a producer of sugar."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ponting_2000_482_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ponting_2000_482-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Sugarcane production was the primary engine of the island's economy, increasing the demand for labour. African slaves were used during portions of the island's history to cultivate sugar cane, and the proportion of imported slaves reached 10% of the total population of Madeira by the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbary_corsairs" title="Barbary corsairs">Barbary corsairs</a> from North Africa, who enslaved Europeans from ships and coastal communities throughout the Mediterranean region, captured 1,200 people in Porto Santo in 1617.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> After the 17th century, as Portuguese sugar production was shifted to <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Portuguese São Tomé and Príncipe">São Tomé and Príncipe</a> and elsewhere, Madeira's most important commodity product became its <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> first amicably occupied the island in 1801 whereafter Colonel <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Clinton" title="William Henry Clinton">William Henry Clinton</a> became governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> A detachment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/85th_Regiment_of_Foot" title="85th Regiment of Foot">85th Regiment of Foot</a> under Lieutenant-colonel <a href="/wiki/James_Willoughby_Gordon" title="James Willoughby Gordon">James Willoughby Gordon</a> garrisoned the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amiens" title="Peace of Amiens">Peace of Amiens</a>, British troops withdrew in 1802, only to reoccupy Madeira in 1807 until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> in 1814.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britishempire.co.uk_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-britishempire.co.uk-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 31 December 1916 during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_War" title="Great War">Great War</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_U-boat" title="German U-boat">German U-boat</a>, <a href="/wiki/SM_U-38" title="SM U-38">SM <i>U-38</i></a>, captained by <a href="/wiki/Max_Valentiner" title="Max Valentiner">Max Valentiner</a>, entered <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a> harbour on Madeira. <i>U-38</i> torpedoed and sank three ships, bringing the war to Portugal by extension. The ships sunk were:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>CS Dacia</i> (1,856 tons), a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> cable-laying vessel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <i>Dacia</i> had previously undertaken war work off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>. It was in the process of diverting the German South American cable into Brest, France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/SS_Kanguroo" title="SS Kanguroo">SS Kanguroo</a></i> (2,493 tons), a French specialized "heavy-lift" transport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Surprise</i> (680 tons), a French <a href="/wiki/Gunboat" title="Gunboat">gunboat</a>. Her commander and 34 crewmen (including 7 Portuguese) were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>After attacking the ships, <i>U-38</i> bombarded Funchal for two hours from a range of about 2 miles (3 km). Batteries on Madeira returned fire and eventually forced <i>U-38</i> to withdraw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 December 1917, two German U-boats, <i><a href="/wiki/SM_U-156" title="SM U-156">SM U-156</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/SM_U-157" title="SM U-157">SM U-157</a></i> (captained by <a href="/wiki/Max_Valentiner" title="Max Valentiner">Max Valentiner</a>), again bombarded Funchal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> This time the attack lasted around 30 minutes. The U-boats fired 40 4.7-and-5.9-inch (120 and 150 mm) shells. There were 3 fatalities and 17 wounded; a number of houses and Santa Clara church were hit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Austria" title="Charles I of Austria">Charles I (Karl I)</a>, the last Emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>, went to Madeira after the war. Determined to prevent an attempt to restore Charles to the throne, the Council of Allied Powers agreed he could go into exile on Madeira because it was isolated in the Atlantic and easily guarded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> He died there on 1 April 1922 and is buried in <a href="/wiki/Monte_(Funchal)" title="Monte (Funchal)">Monte</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomy_and_contemporaneity">Autonomy and contemporaneity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Autonomy and contemporaneity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 July 1976, following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnation_revolution" title="Carnation revolution">democratic revolution</a> of 1974, Portugal granted political autonomy to Madeira, celebrated on <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Day" title="Madeira Day">Madeira Day</a>. The region now has its own government and legislative assembly.</p>
<p>On 20 February 2010 at least 42 people died<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publico26_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-publico26-34">[34]</a></sup> and 100 were injured<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publico21_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-publico21-35">[35]</a></sup> due to an <a href="/wiki/2010_Madeira_floods_and_mudslides" title="2010 Madeira floods and mudslides">extreme weather phenomenon</a> that affected the Island.</p>
<p>In October 2012, it was reported that there was a <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a> epidemic on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> There was a total of 2,168 cases reported of dengue fever since the start in October 2012. The number of cases was on the decline since mid November 2012 and by 4 February 2013, no new cases had been reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2016, wildfires spread on Madeira and reached Funchal, killing three and destroying 150 homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2017, a falling tree killed at least 13 people and injured 49 at a religious ceremony. People had gathered outside a church in a village in the hills - <a href="/wiki/Monte_(Funchal)" title="Monte (Funchal)">Monte</a> - to celebrate the Roman Catholic Feast of the Assumption, which takes place on Tuesday and is a public holiday. The Lady of the Mount festival is the island's biggest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="1194" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg/220px-Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg/330px-Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg/440px-Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_topographic_map-fr.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Distribution of the islands of the archipelago (not including the <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BicaDaCana2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BicaDaCana2.jpg/220px-BicaDaCana2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BicaDaCana2.jpg/330px-BicaDaCana2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BicaDaCana2.jpg/440px-BicaDaCana2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BicaDaCana2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sights from Bica da Cana showing Madeira's high <a href="/wiki/Orography" title="Orography">orography</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The archipelago of Madeira is located 520 km (280 nmi) from the African coast and 1,000 km (540 nmi) from the European continent (approximately a one-and-a-half hour flight from the Portuguese capital of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> It is found in the extreme south of the Tore-Madeira Ridge, a bathymetric structure of great dimensions oriented along a north-northeast to south-southwest axis that extends for 1,000 kilometres (540 nmi). This submarine structure consists of long geomorphological relief that extends from the abyssal plain to 3500 metres; its highest submersed point is at a depth of about 150 metres (around latitude 36ºN). The origins of the Tore-Madeira Ridge are not clearly established, but may have resulted from a morphological <i>buckling</i> of the lithosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands_and_islets">Islands and islets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Islands and islets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madeira (740.7 km²), including Ilhéu de Agostinho, Ilhéu de São Lourenço, Ilhéu Mole (northwest); Total population: 262,456 (2011 Census).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Island" title="Porto Santo Island">Porto Santo</a> (42.5 km²), including <a href="/wiki/Cal_Islet" title="Cal Islet">Ilhéu de Baixo ou da Cal</a>, Ilhéu de Ferro, Ilhéu das Cenouras, Ilhéu de Fora, Ilhéu de Cima; Total population: 5483 (2011 Census).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Desertas_Islands" title="Desertas Islands">Desertas Islands</a> (14.2 km²), including the three uninhabited islands: <a href="/wiki/Deserta_Grande_Island" title="Deserta Grande Island">Deserta Grande Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bugio_Island" title="Bugio Island">Bugio Island</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A3o" title="Chão">Ilhéu de Chão</a>;</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a> (3.6 km²), archipelago 280 km south-southeast of Madeira Island including three main islands and 16 uninhabited islets in two groups: the Northwest Group (<a href="/wiki/Selvagem_Grande_Island" title="Selvagem Grande Island">Selvagem Grande Island</a>, Ilhéu de Palheiro da Terra, Ilhéu de Palheiro do Mar) and the Southeast Group (<a href="/wiki/Selvagem_Pequena_Island" title="Selvagem Pequena Island">Selvagem Pequena Island</a>, Ilhéu Grande, Ilhéu Sul, Ilhéu Pequeno, Ilhéu Fora, Ilhéu Alto, Ilhéu Comprido, Ilhéu Redondo, Ilhéu Norte).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Madeira_Island">Madeira Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Madeira Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Island" title="Madeira Island">Madeira Island</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2998" data-file-width="3147" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg/220px-Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg/330px-Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg/440px-Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madeira%27s_Laurissilva_Forest.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Detailed, true-colour image of Madeira. The image shows that deep green forest <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurissilva" title="Laurissilva">Laurissilva</a></i> survives intact on the steep northern slopes of the island, but in the south, where terrain is gentler, the <a href="/wiki/Terracotta" title="Terracotta">terracotta</a> colour of towns and the light green colour of agriculture are more dominant</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The island of Madeira is at the top of a massive <a href="/wiki/Shield_volcano" title="Shield volcano">shield volcano</a> that rises about 6 km (20,000 ft) from the floor of the Atlantic Ocean, on the Tore underwater mountain range. The volcano formed atop an east-west <a href="/wiki/Rift" title="Rift">rift</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">oceanic crust</a> along the <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">African Plate</a>, beginning during the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> epoch over 5 million years ago, continuing into the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> until about 700,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GVP_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-GVP-46">[46]</a></sup> This was followed by extensive <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a>, producing two large amphitheatres open to south in the central part of the island. Volcanic activity later resumed, producing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scoria_cone" title="Scoria cone">scoria cones</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lava_flow" title="Lava flow">lava flows</a> atop the older eroded shield. The most recent volcanic eruptions were on the west-central part of the island only 6,500 years ago, creating more <a href="/wiki/Cinder_cone" title="Cinder cone">cinder cones</a> and lava flows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GVP_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-GVP-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is the largest island of the group with an area of 741 km<sup>2</sup> (286 sq mi), a length of 57 km (35 mi) (from Ponte de São Lourenço to Ponte do Pargo), while approximately 22 km (14 mi) at its widest point (from Ponte da Cruz to Ponte São Jorge), with a coastline of 150 km (90 mi). It has a mountain ridge that extends along the centre of the island, reaching 1,862 metres (6,109 feet) at its highest point (<a href="/wiki/Pico_Ruivo" title="Pico Ruivo">Pico Ruivo</a>), while much lower (below 200 metres) along its eastern extent. The primitive volcanic foci responsible for the central mountainous area, consisted of the peaks: Ruivo (1,862 m), Torres (1,851 m), Arieiro (1,818 m), Cidrão (1,802 m), Cedro (1,759 m), Casado (1,725 m), Grande (1,657 m), Ferreiro (1,582 m). At the end of this eruptive phase, an island circled by reefs was formed, its marine vestiges are evident in a calcareous layer in the area of Lameiros, in São Vicente (which was later explored for <a href="/wiki/Calcium_oxide" title="Calcium oxide">calcium oxide</a> production). Sea cliffs, such as <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Gir%C3%A3o" title="Cabo Girão">Cabo Girão</a>, valleys and ravines extend from this central spine, making the interior generally inaccessible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Daily life is concentrated in the many villages at the mouths of the ravines, through which the heavy rains of autumn and winter usually travel to the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Madeira has been classified as a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>Csa</i>/<i>Csb</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Based on differences in sun exposure, humidity, and annual mean temperature, there are clear variations between north- and south-facing regions, as well as between some islands. The islands are strongly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canary_Current" title="Canary Current">Canary Current</a>, giving mild year-round temperatures; according to the Instituto de Meteorologia (IM), the average annual temperature at Funchal weather station is 19.6 °C (67.3 °F) for the 1980–2010 period. Porto Santo has at least one weather station with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semiarid_climate" title="Semiarid climate">semiarid climate</a> (<i>BSh</i>). On the highest windward slopes of Madeira, rainfall exceeds 1,250 mm (50 inches) per year, mostly falling between October and April. In most winters snowfall occurs in the mountains of Madeira.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildfires">Wildfires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Wildfires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="912" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg/220px-Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg/330px-Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg/440px-Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_amo_2012201_lrg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
NASA satellite image of wildfires on the island of Madeira from 19 July 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Drought conditions, coupled with hot and windy weather in summer, have caused numerous wildfires in recent years. The largest of the fires in August 2010 burned through 95 percent of the Funchal Ecological Park, a 1,000-hectare preserve set aside to restore native vegetation to the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In July 2012 Madeira was suffering again from severe drought. Wildfires broke out on 18 July, in the midst of temperatures up to 40 °C (more than 100 °F) and high winds. By 20 July, fires had spread to the nearby island of Porto Santo, and firefighters were sent from mainland Portugal to contain the multiple blazes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2013, a hospital and some private homes were evacuated as a wildfire approached Funchal. A number of homes were destroyed when the fire hit Monte, a suburb of Funchal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2016, wildfires caused over 1,000 people to be evacuated, and led to the death of three people - all of which are said to have been elderly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The wildfires threatened the capital of Madeira -<a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a> - specifically, however other administrative regions of Madeira were also threatened by separate wildfires - e.g. <a href="/wiki/Calheta,_Madeira" title="Calheta, Madeira">Calheta</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_Fauna">Flora and Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Flora and Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the south, there is very little left of the indigenous subtropical rainforest which once covered the whole island<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (the original settlers set fire to the island to clear the land for farming) and gave it the name it now bears (<i>Madeira</i> means "wood" in Portuguese). However, in the north, the valleys contain native trees of fine growth. These <a href="/wiki/Laurel_forest" title="Laurel forest">"laurisilva" forests</a>, called <i>lauraceas madeirense</i>, notably the forests on the northern slopes of Madeira Island, are designated as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.The paleobotanical record of Madeira reveals that laurissilva forests has existed in this island for at least 1.8 million years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>. The critically endangered vine <i><a href="/wiki/Jasminum_azoricum" title="Jasminum azoricum">Jasminum azoricum</a></i> is one of the plant species that is endemic to Madeira.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCN_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-64">[64]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Madeiran_Wall_Lizard">Madeiran Wall Lizard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Madeiran Wall Lizard">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg/220px-Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg/330px-Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg/440px-Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teira_dugesii_k7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madeiran wall lizard (<i>Lacerta dugesii</i>) captured in <a href="/wiki/Levada" title="Levada">Levada do Norte</a>, Madeira</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lacerta_dugesii" title="Lacerta dugesii">Lacerta dugesii</a></div>
<p>The Madeiran wall lizard (<i>Lacerta dugesii</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lizard" title="Lizard">lizard</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lacertidae" title="Lacertidae">Lacertidae</a> <a href="/wiki/Family_(biology)" title="Family (biology)">family</a>. The species is <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to the Island where is very common being and the only small lizard, ranging from sea coasts to altitudes of 1,850 metres (6,070 ft). It is usually found in rocky places or among scrub and may climb into trees. It is also found in gardens and on the walls of buildings. It feeds on small invertebrates such as ants and also eats some vegetable matter. The tail is easily shed and the stump regenerates slowly. Females lay two to three clutches of eggs in a year with the juveniles being about 3 cm (1.2 in) when they hatch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-65">[65]</a></sup> The colouring is variable and tends to match the colour of the animal's surroundings, being some shade of brown or grey with occasionally a greenish tinge. Most animals are finely flecked with darker markings. The underparts are white or cream, sometimes with dark spots, with some males having orange or red underparts and blue throats, but these bright colours may fade if the animal is disturbed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-65">[65]</a></sup> The Madeiran wall lizard grows to a snout-to-vent length of about 8 cm (3.1 in) with a tail about 1.7 times the length of its body. Females lay two to three clutches of eggs in a year with the juveniles being about 3 cm (1.2 in) when they hatch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Levadas">Levadas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Levadas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Levada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="1224" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Levada.jpg/170px-Levada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Levada.jpg/255px-Levada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Levada.jpg/340px-Levada.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Levada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Levada" title="Levada">levada</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levadas" title="Levadas">Levadas</a></div>
<p>The island of Madeira is wet in the northwest but dry in the southeast. In the 16th century the Portuguese started building levadas or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(watercourse)" title="Aqueduct (watercourse)">aqueducts</a> to carry water to the agricultural regions in the south. Madeira is very mountainous, and building the levadas was difficult and often sentenced criminals or slaves were used.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many are cut into the sides of mountains, and it was also necessary to dig 25 miles (40 km) of tunnels, some of which are still accessible.</p>
<p>Today the levadas not only supply water to the southern parts of the island but provide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydro-electric_power" title="Hydro-electric power">hydro-electric power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> There are over 1,350 miles (2,170 km) of levadas and they provide a network of walking paths. Some provide easy and relaxing walks through the countryside, but others are narrow, crumbling ledges where a slip could result in serious injury or death.</p>
<p>Two of the most popular levadas to hike are the <i>Levada do Caldeirão Verde</i> and the <i>Levada do Caldeirão do Inferno</i> which should not be attempted by hikers prone to vertigo or without torches and helmets. The <i>Levada do Caniçal</i> is a much easier walk, running 7.1 miles (11.4 km) from Maroços to the <i>Caniçal Tunnel</i>. It is known as the <i>mimosa levada</i> because <a href="/wiki/Mimosa" title="Mimosa">mimosa trees</a> are found all along the route.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
