<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funchal">Funchal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Funchal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_27_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3651" data-file-width="7303" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Madeira_27_2014.jpg/300px-Madeira_27_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Madeira_27_2014.jpg/450px-Madeira_27_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Madeira_27_2014.jpg/600px-Madeira_27_2014.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_27_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Partial view of the capital as seen from the mountains above it</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Funchal is the capital and principal city of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region" title="Autonomous Region">Autonomous Region</a> of Madeira, located along the southern coast of the island of Madeira. It is a modern city, located within a natural geological "<a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre" title="Amphitheatre">amphitheatre</a>" composed of vulcanological structure and fluvial hydrological forces. Beginning at the harbour (Porto de Funchal), the neighbourhoods and streets rise almost 1,200 metres (3,900 ft), along gentle slopes that helped to provide a natural shelter to the early settlers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Madeira" title="Demographics of Madeira">Demographics of Madeira</a></div>
<p>The island was settled by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese people</a>, especially farmers from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minho_(province)" title="Minho (province)">Minho</a> region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> meaning that <i>Madeirans</i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt"><i>Madeirenses</i></span>), as they are called, are ethnically Portuguese, though they have developed their own distinct regional identity and cultural traits.</p>
<p>The region has a total population of just under 270,000, the majority of whom live on the main island of Madeira where the population density is 337/km²; meanwhile only around 5,000 live on the <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Island" title="Porto Santo Island">Porto Santo Island</a> where the population density is 112/km².</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_diaspora" title="Portuguese diaspora">Portuguese diaspora</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1358" data-file-width="2206" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the European Union in the world, with overseas countries and territories (OCT) and outermost regions (OMR) for which Madeira is included</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madeirans migrated to the United States, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, British Guiana, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Madeiran immigrants in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> mostly clustered in the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">mid-Atlantic states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Northern California, and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. The city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Bedford" title="New Bedford">New Bedford</a> is especially rich in Madeirans, hosting the Museum of Madeira Heritage, as well as the annual Madeiran and Luso-American celebration, the Feast of the Blessed Sacrament, the world's largest celebration of Madeiran heritage, regularly drawing crowds of tens of thousands to the city's Madeira Field.</p>
<p>In 1846, when a famine struck Madeira over 6,000 of the inhabitants migrated to <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a>. In 1891 they numbered 4.3% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In 1902 in <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> there were 5,000 Portuguese people, mostly Madeirans. In 1910 this grew to 21,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_Hawaii_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress_Hawaii-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>1849 saw an emigration of Protestant religious exiles from Madeira to the United States, by way of Trinidad and other locations in the West Indies. Most of them settled in <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> with financial and physical aid of the American Protestant Society, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. In the late 1830s the Reverend <a href="/wiki/Robert_Reid_Kalley" title="Robert Reid Kalley">Robert Reid Kalley</a>, from Scotland, a Presbyterian minister as well as a physician, made a stop at Funchal, Madeira on his way to a mission in China, with his wife, so that she could recover from an illness. The Rev. Kalley and his wife stayed on Madeira where he began preaching the Protestant gospel and converting islanders from Catholicism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Eventually, the Rev. Kalley was arrested for his religious conversion activities and imprisoned. Another missionary from Scotland, William Hepburn Hewitson, took on Protestant ministerial activities in Madeira. By 1846, about 1,000 Protestant Madeirenses, who were discriminated against and the subjects of mob violence because of their religious conversions, chose to immigrate to Trinidad and other locations in the West Indies in answer for a call for sugar plantation workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The Madeirenses exiles did not fare well in the West Indies. The tropical climate was unfamiliar and they found themselves in serious economic difficulties. By 1848, the American Protestant Society raised money and sent the Rev. Manuel J. Gonsalves, a Baptist minister and a naturalized U.S. citizen from Madeira, to work with the Rev. Arsenio da Silva, who had emigrated with the exiles from Madeira, to arrange to resettle those who wanted to come to the United States. The Rev. da Silva died in early 1849. Later in 1849, the Rev. Gonsalves was then charged with escorting the exiles from Trinidad to be settled in Sangamon and Morgan counties in Illinois on land purchased with funds raised by the American Protestant Society. Accounts state that anywhere from 700 to 1,000 exiles came to the United States at this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are several large Madeiran communities around the world, such as the great number in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">UK</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_British" title="Portuguese British">Portuguese British</a> community mostly made up of Madeirans celebrate <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Day" title="Madeira Day">Madeira Day</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The setting-up of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_trade_zone" title="Free trade zone">free trade zone</a> has led to the installation, under more favourable conditions, of infrastructure, production shops and essential services for small and medium-sized industrial enterprises. The Madeira Free Trade Zone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> also called the Madeira International Business Centre, being a tax-privileged economic area, provides an incentive for companies, offering them financial and tax advantages via a whole range of activities exercised in the Industrial Free Zone, the Off-Shore Financial Centre, the International Shipping Register organisation, and the International Service Centre.</p>
<p>Madeira has been a significant recipient of <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> aid, totalling up to €2 billion. In 2012, it was reported that despite a population of just 250,000, the local administration owes some €6 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_Beach_(163610932).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg/200px-Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg/300px-Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg/400px-Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madeira_Beach_(163610932).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calheta_beach" title="Calheta beach">manufactured coastal beach</a> of <a href="/wiki/Calheta,_Madeira" title="Calheta, Madeira">Calheta</a>: replacing the dark rock/sand of the volcanic island with beach sand.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Portugal" title="Tourism in Portugal">Tourism</a> is an important sector in the region's economy since it contributes 20%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> to the region's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>, providing support throughout the year for commercial, transport and other activities and constituting a significant market for local products. The share in Gross Value Added of hotels and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restaurants" title="Restaurants">restaurants</a> (9%) also highlights this phenomenon. The island of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porto_Santo" title="Porto Santo">Porto Santo</a>, with its 9 km (5.6 mi) long beach and its climate, is entirely devoted to tourism.</p>
<p>Visitors are mainly from the European Union, with German, British, Scandinavian and Portuguese tourists providing the main contingents. The average annual occupancy rate was 60.3% in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> reaching its maximum in March and April, when it exceeds 70%.</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Whale_watching">Whale watching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Whale watching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">Whale watching</a> has become very popular in recent years. Many species of dolphins such as <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">common dolphin</a>, spotted dolphin, <a href="/wiki/Striped_dolphin" title="Striped dolphin">striped dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Short-finned_pilot_whale" title="Short-finned pilot whale">short-finned pilot whale</a>, and whales such as <a href="/wiki/Bryde%27s_whale" title="Bryde's whale">Bryde's whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sei_whale" title="Sei whale">Sei whale</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beaked_whale" title="Beaked whale">beaked whales</a> can be spotted near the coast or offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madeira is part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>.</p>
<p>In 2009, there were 7,105 legal immigrants living in Madeira Islands. They come mostly from <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (1,300), the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (912), <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (732) and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (682), according to Serviço de Estrangeiros e Fronteiras (SEF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEFSTAT_.E2.80.93_Portal_de_Estat.C3.ADstica_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-SEFSTAT_.E2.80.93_Portal_de_Estat.C3.ADstica-89">[89]</a></sup> In 2013, that number dropped to 5,829, also according to SEF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEFSTAT_.E2.80.93_Portal_de_Estat.C3.ADstica_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-SEFSTAT_.E2.80.93_Portal_de_Estat.C3.ADstica-89">[89]</a></sup> The latest figures available (2015) detail another slight drop to 5,745, the majority of which are from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (818), <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (752) and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (581).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEFSTAT_.E2.80.93_Portal_de_Estat.C3.ADstica_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-SEFSTAT_.E2.80.93_Portal_de_Estat.C3.ADstica-89">[89]</a></sup> The ongoing crisis in Venezuela has increased the flux of immigrants from the nation particularly from those with double citizenship (former Madeira immigrants).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Electricity on Madeira is provided solely through EEM - Empresa de Electricidade da Madeira, SA - who hold a monopoly for the provision of electrical supply on the autonomous region - and consists largely of fossil fuels, but with a significant supply of seasonal hydroelectricity from the Levada system, wind power and a small amount of solar. In 2011, renewable energy formed 26.5% of the electricity used in Madeira.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Madeira" title="Transport in Madeira">Transport in Madeira</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG/200px-Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG/300px-Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG/400px-Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> makes daily trips between Madeira and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porto_Santo" title="Porto Santo">Porto Santo</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Islands have two airports, <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo_International_Airport" title="Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport">Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Airport" title="Porto Santo Airport">Porto Santo Airport</a>, on the islands of Madeira and Porto Santo respectively. From Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport the most frequent flights are to <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>. There are also direct flights to over 30 other airports in Europe and nearby islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Transport between the two main islands is by plane, or ferries from the Porto Santo Line,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> the latter also carrying vehicles. Visiting the interior of the islands is now easy thanks to construction of the <i>Vias Rápidas</i>, major roads that cross the island. Modern roads reach all points of interest on the islands.</p>
<p>Funchal has an extensive public transportation system. Bus companies, including <a href="/wiki/Hor%C3%A1rios_do_Funchal" title="Horários do Funchal">Horários do Funchal</a> which has been operating for over a hundred years, have regularly scheduled routes to all points of interest on the island.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madeirenses.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Madeirenses.jpg/200px-Madeirenses.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Madeirenses.jpg/300px-Madeirenses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Madeirenses.jpg/400px-Madeirenses.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madeirenses.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bailinho da Madeira</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">Folklore</a> music in Madeira is widespread and mainly uses local musical instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Machete_(musical_instrument)" title="Machete (musical instrument)">machete</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajao" title="Rajao">rajao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brinquinho" title="Brinquinho">brinquinho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cavaquinho" title="Cavaquinho">cavaquinho</a>, which are used in traditional folkloric dances like the <i>bailinho da Madeira</i>.</p>
<p>Emigrants from Madeira also influenced the creation of new musical instruments. In the 1880s, the <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a> was created, based on two small guitar-like instruments of Madeiran origin, the <a href="/wiki/Cavaquinho" title="Cavaquinho">cavaquinho</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajao" title="Rajao">rajao</a>. The ukulele was introduced to the Hawaiian Islands by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> immigrants from Madeira and Cape Verde.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Three immigrants in particular, Madeiran cabinet makers Manuel Nunes, José do Espírito Santo, and Augusto Dias, are generally credited as the first ukulele makers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Two weeks after they disembarked from the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ravenscrag_(ship)" title="Ravenscrag (ship)">SS Ravenscrag</a></i> in late August 1879, the <i>Hawaiian Gazette</i> reported that "Madeira Islanders recently arrived here, have been delighting the people with nightly street concerts."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2664" data-file-width="4000" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg/200px-Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg/300px-Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg/400px-Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Lapas", the true limpet species <i><a href="/wiki/Patella_vulgata" title="Patella vulgata">Patella vulgata</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because of the geographic situation of Madeira in the Atlantic Ocean, the island has an abundance of fish of various kinds. The species that are consumed the most are espada (<a href="/wiki/Black_scabbardfish" title="Black scabbardfish">black scabbardfish</a>), <a href="/wiki/Thunnus" title="Thunnus">blue fin tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_marlin" title="White marlin">white marlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_blue_marlin" title="Atlantic blue marlin">blue marlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albacore" title="Albacore">albacore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bigeye_tuna" title="Bigeye tuna">bigeye tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wahoo" title="Wahoo">wahoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">spearfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_tuna" title="Skipjack tuna">skipjack tuna</a> and many others are found in the local dishes as they are found up and down the coast of Madeira.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Espada is often served with <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">Bacalhau</a> is also popular, as it is in Portugal.</p>
<p>There are many meat dishes on Madeira, one of the most popular being <a href="/wiki/Espetada" title="Espetada">espetada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Espetada is traditionally made of large chunks of beef rubbed in garlic, salt and bay leaf and marinated for 4 to 6 hours in Madeira wine, red wine vinegar and olive oil then skewered onto a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bay_laurel" title="Bay laurel">bay laurel</a> stick and left to grill over smouldering wood chips. These are so integral a part of traditional eating habits that a special iron stand is available with a T-shaped end, each branch of the "T" having a slot in the middle to hold a <a href="/wiki/Brochette" title="Brochette">brochette</a> (espeto in Portuguese); a small plate is then placed underneath to collect the juices. The brochettes are very long and have a V-shaped blade in order to pierce the meat more easily. It is usually accompanied with the local bread called <a href="/wiki/Bolo_do_caco" title="Bolo do caco">bolo do caco</a>.</p>
<p>Other popular dishes in Madeira include <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A7orda" title="Açorda">açorda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feijoada" title="Feijoada">feijoada</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carne_de_Vinha_d%27_Alhos" title="Carne de Vinha d' Alhos">carne de vinha d'alhos</a>.</p>
<p>Traditional pastries in Madeira usually contain local ingredients, one of the most common being <i>mel de cana</i>, literally "sugarcane honey" (<a href="/wiki/Molasses" title="Molasses">molasses</a>). The traditional cake of Madeira is called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolo_de_Mel" title="Bolo de Mel">Bolo de Mel</a></i>, which translates as (Sugarcane) "Honey Cake" and according to custom, is never cut with a knife, but broken into pieces by hand. It is a rich and heavy cake. The cake commonly well known as "<a href="/wiki/Madeira_cake" title="Madeira cake">Madeira Cake</a>" in England also finds its naming roots in the Island of Madeira.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malasada" title="Malasada">Malasadas</a> are a Madeiran creation which were taken around the world by emigrants to places such as <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. In Madeira, <a href="/wiki/Malasada" title="Malasada">Malasadas</a> are mainly consumed during the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Madeira" title="Carnival of Madeira">Carnival of Madeira</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pastel_de_nata" title="Pastel de nata">Pastéis de nata</a>, as in the rest of Portugal, are also very popular.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milho_Frito" title="Milho Frito">Milho frito</a> is a very popular dish in Madeira which is very similar to the Italian dish <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a>. <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A7orda" title="Açorda">Açorda</a> Madeirense is another popular local dish.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beverages">Beverages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Beverages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Madeira_wine" title="Madeira wine">Madeira wine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG/200px-Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG/300px-Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG/400px-Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bottles of Madeira labelled by the different grape varieties used to produce the many styles of wine</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CORAL.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="314" data-file-width="112" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/CORAL.jpg/100px-CORAL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7f/CORAL.jpg 1.5x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CORAL.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coral Beer, produced since 1872<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> in the Island's main brewery, has achieved several <a href="/wiki/Monde_Selection" title="Monde Selection">Monde Selection</a> medals</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madeira is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fortified_(wine)" title="Fortified (wine)">fortified wine</a>, produced in the Madeira Islands; varieties may be sweet or dry. It has a history dating back to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a> when Madeira was a standard <a href="/wiki/Port#Port_of_call" title="Port">port of call</a> for ships heading to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> or <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>. To prevent the wine from spoiling, neutral <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grape_spirit" title="Grape spirit">grape spirits</a> were added. However, wine producers of Madeira discovered, when an unsold shipment of wine returned to the islands after a round trip, that the flavour of the wine had been transformed by exposure to heat and movement. Today, Madeira is noted for its unique winemaking process which involves heating the wine and deliberately exposing the wine to some levels of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxidation" title="Oxidation">oxidation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sotheby_pg_340.E2.80.93341_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sotheby_pg_340.E2.80.93341-98">[98]</a></sup> Most countries limit the use of the term <i>Madeira</i> to those wines that come from the Madeira Islands, to which the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> grants <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protected_designation_of_origin" title="Protected designation of origin">Protected Designation of Origin</a> (PDO) status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>A local beer called Coral is produced by the <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Brewery" title="Madeira Brewery">Madeira Brewery</a>, which dates from 1872. It has achieved 2 <a href="/wiki/Monde_Selection" title="Monde Selection">Monde Selection</a> Grand Gold Medals, 24 Monde Selection Gold Medals and 2 Monde Selection Silver Medals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Other alcoholic drinks are also popular in Madeira, such as the locally created <a href="/wiki/Poncha" title="Poncha">Poncha</a>, Niquita, Pé de Cabra, Aniz, as well as Portuguese drinks such as <a href="/wiki/Macieira_Brandy" title="Macieira Brandy">Macieira Brandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Licor_Beir%C3%A3o" title="Licor Beirão">Licor Beirão</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Laranjada" title="Laranjada">Laranjada</a> is a type of <a href="/wiki/Carbonation" title="Carbonation">carbonated</a> soft drink with an orange flavour, its name being derived from the Portuguese word <i>laranja</i> ("orange"). Launched in 1872 it was the first <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drink</a> to be produced in Portugal, and remains very popular to the present day. <a href="/wiki/Brisa_drink" title="Brisa drink">Brisa drinks</a>, a brand name, are also very popular and come in a range of flavours.</p>
<p>There is also a huge coffee culture in Madeira. Like in mainland Portugal, popular coffee-based drinks include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garoto_Coffee" title="Garoto Coffee">Garoto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A3o" title="Galão">Galão</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bica_Coffee" title="Bica Coffee">Bica</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_com_Cheirinho" title="Café com Cheirinho">Café com Cheirinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazagran_(coffee_beverage)" title="Mazagran (coffee beverage)">Mazagran</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinesa" title="Chinesa">Chinesa</a> and many more.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Madeira" title="Sport in Madeira">Sport in Madeira</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_provinces">Sister provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sister provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Madeira Island has the following sister provinces:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><img alt="Italy" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">Autonomous Region of Aosta Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (1987)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey"><img alt="Jersey" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flag_of_Jersey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Jersey.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flag_of_Jersey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Jersey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flag_of_Jersey.svg/46px-Flag_of_Jersey.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Jersey" title="Bailiwick of Jersey">Bailiwick of Jersey</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Crown_Dependencies" title="British Crown Dependencies">British Crown Dependencies</a> (1998)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa"><img alt="South Africa" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape_Province" title="Eastern Cape Province">Eastern Cape Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea"><img alt="South Korea" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Jeju_Province" title="Jeju Province">Jeju Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (2007)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar"><img alt="Gibraltar" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg/23px-Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg/35px-Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg/46px-Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> (2009) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Postage_stamps">Postage stamps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Postage stamps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamps_and_postal_history_of_Madeira" title="Postage stamps and postal history of Madeira">Postage stamps and postal history of Madeira</a></div>
<p>Portugal has issued <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamp" title="Postage stamp">postage stamps</a> for Madeira during several periods, beginning in 1868.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal,_10th_June_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="2810" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg/170px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg/255px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg/340px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal,_10th_June_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, born in Madeira, was the 2008, 2013, 2014 and 2016 <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="FIFA Ballon d'Or">World Player of the Year</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joe_berardo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2896" data-file-width="1944" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Joe_berardo.jpg/170px-Joe_berardo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Joe_berardo.jpg/255px-Joe_berardo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Joe_berardo.jpg/340px-Joe_berardo.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joe_berardo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Joe_Berardo" title="Joe Berardo">Joe Berardo</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Businessman" title="Businessman">businessman</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stock_investor" title="Stock investor">stock investor</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speculator" title="Speculator">speculator</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_collector" title="Art collector">art collector</a>. He is also one of the wealthiest people in Portugal.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The following people were either born or have lived part of their lives in Madeira:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_Berardo" title="Joe Berardo">Joe Berardo</a>, Portuguese millionaire, and art collector</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rubina_Berardo" title="Rubina Berardo">Rubina Berardo</a>, Portuguese politician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Abreu" title="António de Abreu">António de Abreu</a>, naval officer and navigator</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nadia_Almada" title="Nadia Almada">Nadia Almada</a>, a winner of the British reality show <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Brother_2004_(UK)" title="Big Brother 2004 (UK)">Big Brother</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Menasseh_Ben_Israel" title="Menasseh Ben Israel">Menasseh Ben Israel</a>, Jewish Rabbi.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Austria" title="Charles I of Austria">Charles I of Austria</a>, deposed monarch, died in exile on Madeira in 1922</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catarina_Fagundes" title="Catarina Fagundes">Catarina Fagundes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> athlete for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windsurf" title="Windsurf">windsurf</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A2nia_Fernandes" title="Vânia Fernandes">Vânia Fernandes</a>, Portuguese singer who represented Portugal in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurovision_2008" title="Eurovision 2008">Eurovision 2008</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vicente_de_Freitas" title="José Vicente de Freitas">José Vicente de Freitas</a>, military general and politician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_Rodrigues" title="Vasco da Gama Rodrigues">Vasco da Gama Rodrigues</a>, poet, born in <a href="/wiki/Paul_do_Mar" title="Paul do Mar">Paul do Mar</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teod%C3%B3sio_Clemente_de_Gouveia" title="Teodósio Clemente de Gouveia">Teodósio Clemente de Gouveia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinal</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Walter_Grabham" title="George Walter Grabham">George Walter Grabham</a>, geologist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Herberto_H%C3%A9lder" title="Herberto Hélder">Herberto Hélder</a>, poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mois%C3%A9s_Henriques" title="Moisés Henriques">Moisés Henriques</a>, former Australian Under-19 Captain and current <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_cricket_team" title="New South Wales cricket team">NSW Blues</a> and Australian international <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> cricketer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alberto_Jo%C3%A3o_Jardim" title="Alberto João Jardim">Alberto João Jardim</a>, second President of the Regional Government</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Jardim" title="Luis Jardim">Luís Jardim</a>, producer of music</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Langerhans" title="Paul Langerhans">Paul Langerhans</a>, German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathologist" title="Pathologist">pathologist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biologist" title="Biologist">biologist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A1tima_Lopes" title="Fátima Lopes">Fátima Lopes</a>, fashion designer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jaime_Ornelas_Camacho" title="Jaime Ornelas Camacho">Jaime Ornelas Camacho</a>, <i>first and former</i> President of the Regional Government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aires_de_Ornelas_e_Vasconcelos" title="Aires de Ornelas e Vasconcelos">Aires de Ornelas e Vasconcelos</a>, former Archbishop of the former Portuguese colonial enclave <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> (in India)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Mathews" title="Lloyd Mathews">Lloyd Mathews</a>, British naval officer, politician and abolitionist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pestana_Group" title="Pestana Group">Dionísio Pestana</a>, president of the <a href="/wiki/Pestana_Group" title="Pestana Group">Pestana Group</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rigo_23" title="Rigo 23">Rigo 23</a>, artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Rodrigues_(sailor)" title="João Rodrigues (sailor)">João Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windsurfer" title="Windsurfer">windsurfer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> and former <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> football player</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Santos" title="John Santos">John Santos</a>, photographer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ana_da_Silva" title="Ana da Silva">Ana da Silva</a>, founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Post-punk" title="Post-punk">post-punk</a> band <a href="/wiki/The_Raincoats" title="The Raincoats">The Raincoats</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pedro_Camacho" title="Pedro Camacho">Pedro Macedo Camacho</a>, composer</li>
<li>Flávia Brito, Miss Universo Portugal 2016, beauty pageant</li>
<li>Manoel Dias Soeyro or <a href="/wiki/Menasseh_Ben_Israel" title="Menasseh Ben Israel">Menasseh Ben Israel</a> (1604–1657), <a href="/wiki/Spanish_and_Portuguese_Jews" title="Spanish and Portuguese Jews">Sephardi</a> <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">Rabbi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publisher" title="Publisher">publisher</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Artur_de_Sousa_Pinga" title="Artur de Sousa Pinga">Artur de Sousa Pinga</a>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CS_Mar%C3%ADtimo" title="CS Marítimo">CS Marítimo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Futebol_Clube_do_Porto" title="Futebol Clube do Porto">FC Porto</a> football player</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maximiano_de_Sousa_(Max)" title="Maximiano de Sousa (Max)">Maximiano de Sousa (Max)</a>, popular singer, born in <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virg%C3%ADlio_Delgado_Teixeira" title="Virgílio Delgado Teixeira">Virgílio Teixeira</a>, actor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Travassos_Valdez,_1st_Count_of_Bonfim" title="José Travassos Valdez, 1st Count of Bonfim">José Travassos Valdez, 1st Count of Bonfim</a>, governor during 1827–1828</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miguel_Albuquerque" title="Miguel Albuquerque">Miguel Albuquerque</a>, third and current President of the Regional Government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Sousa" title="Bernardo Sousa">Bernardo Sousa</a>, rally driver in the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">WRC</a></li>
</ul>
